Distinguishing Hamd and Shukr
Author defines hamd and shukr and explains their general-specific relationship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between hamd and shukr based on their conventional definitions and identify their general-specific relationship.

Core Idea
Hamd is praise for praiseworthy qualities; shukr is using Allah's favors in obedience — they intersect but are not identical.

This lesson examines two key terms: hamd (praise) and shukr (gratitude). The author clarifies their conventional meanings and explains how they relate as 'umum wa khusus min wajh' — a partial overlap. Understanding this distinction is crucial for accurate theological discourse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of hamd
Locate the conventional definition of hamd in the Arabic passage. The author defines it as 'an action that informs about glorification of the praised one'. Note that the OCR is damaged; the intended definition likely involves informing about praiseworthy attributes.
The exact wording may be 'فعل يُنبئ عن تعظيم المُنعِم' (informing about glorifying the Bestower).
2
Identify the definition of shukr
Find the definition of shukr: 'the servant expending all of Allah's favors in that which He created them for, i.e., obedience'. This is an active utilization of blessings.
3
Find the common element
Both hamd and shukr involve recognizing and honoring Allah. The passage states they have a 'general and specific from one aspect' relationship — they meet in some respects (e.g., both are forms of acknowledgment).
4
Identify the differences
The author mentions two points of difference: the source (al-mawarid) and the object (al-muta‘allaq). The source of hamd is a praiseworthy attribute; the source of shukr is a favor received. The object of hamd is the possessor of the attribute; the object of shukr is the benefactor.
Shukr is more specific because it requires using the favor in obedience.
5
Summarize the relationship
Hamd and shukr are not identical but overlap. This is called 'umum wa khusus min wajh' (general and specific from one aspect). You now have a tool for analyzing similar term pairs in Islamic sciences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحمد عرفا فعل ينهي عن تعظيم النبي بسبب كونه مني او هوسا؟ و لشكر لقد عالي الاشهر وبينها وبين الحمد لله عموم وخصوص من وجه فير مهما باعتبار الموراد و علومه باعتبار المتعلق والشكر عر فا صرف العبد جميع ملا تو الله به علي متى سمع وعين الي ما خالق للجله وهو الخص مطلق من كل واحد من الثلاثة قبله وهذا هو الشكر الماموريه شرعا
And hamd, conventionally, is an action that informs about the glorification of the Prophet because he is from me or he is a qualifier? And shukr, indeed it is well-known [that] between it and hamd there is a general and specific relation from one aspect, [they differ] in terms of the source and in terms of the object. And shukr, conventionally, is the servant spending all the favors that Allah has given him upon what He created for the sake of Him, and it is more specific absolutely than each of the three before. And this is the shukr commanded by shari'ah.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage defines two related terms: hamd (praise) and shukr (gratitude), and explains their relationship. The author begins by giving the conventional definition of hamd. According to the text, hamd is an action that informs about the glorification of the praised one. However, the OCR is unclear here — it may actually be 'فعل يُنبئ عن تعظيم المنعم' (an action that informs about glorifying the bestower of favors). Then the author turns to shukr, stating that it is well-known among scholars that there is a 'general and specific from one aspect' relation between the two. They differ in two ways: in terms of the source (al-mawarid) and in terms of the object (al-muta‘allaq). The source of hamd is the praiseworthy attribute itself, while the source of shukr is the favor received. The object of hamd is the person possessing the attribute, whereas the object of shukr is the benefactor. Then the author defines shukr conventionally: it is the servant expending all of Allah's favors (such as hearing, sight, and other faculties) in what Allah created them for, i.e., obedience to Him. Thus shukr is more specific than hamd, as it requires the use of favors in obedience. The author clarifies that this is the shukr commanded in shari'ah.

D) A feeling of appreciation in the heart.

Key Takeaway
Hamd and shukr are related but distinct: hamd is praise for praiseworthy attributes, while shukr is active use of favors in obedience; they overlap in praising Allah but differ in source and object.

The Definition and Classification Dispute of Isti'ara
Author defines isti'ara and discusses the disagreement between jumhur and al-Amidi regarding its classification as tashbih baligh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two competing classifications of isti'ara and explain the basis of the dispute between the majority and al-Amidi.

Core Idea
Isti'ara may be classified as eloquent simile, but al-Amidi challenges this categorization.

This lesson explores the definition of explicit metaphor (isti'ara musarrah) and the scholarly disagreement about its logical classification. The majority of grammarians argue that isti'ara is a type of eloquent simile (tashbih baligh), while al-Amidi dissents. Understanding this dispute reveals how even figurative language is subject to rigorous logical analysis in the Islamic tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its definition
Find the term being defined (isti'ara musarrah) in the passage. Note the example about Zayd: something is attributed to him that is perceived only by the intellect, expressed through a revealing utterance.
The example illustrates how explicit metaphor works: a borrowed term clearly states the comparison.
2
Extract the majority position
The majority (al-Jumhur) asserts that isti'ara must be classified under tashbih baligh (eloquent simile). This means they consider metaphor a compressed form of simile.
The phrase 'قالت الجمهور يجب ان يكون من باب التشبيه البليغ' is key.
3
Identify the dissenting position
Al-Amidi disagrees with the majority. The passage hints that for him, isti'ara is not necessarily tashbih baligh; it may be a separate category.
The phrase 'والامر ان يكونان' suggests two possibilities: either it is tashbih baligh or something else.
4
Understand the logical significance
This is not merely a linguistic debate. How isti'ara is classified affects its role in argumentation: if it is a type of simile, it carries certain logical implications; if separate, it may function differently in definitions and proofs.
Think about how metaphors are used in theological and juristic reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاستعارة المصرية على الخلاف بين الجمهور والآمدي في مصر زيد امتد حيث نمها له الذي حك الإنسان بالمنطلق المفصح عما في الضمير من المكنونات قالت الجمهور يجب ان يكون من باب التشبيه البليغ والامر ان يكونان
The explicit metaphor is subject to a disagreement between the majority (al-Jumhur) and al-Amidi regarding the case of Zayd, where it was attributed to him that which the human intellect perceives through the revealing expression of what is in the inner consciousness. The majority said it must be from the category of eloquent simile (tashbih baligh), and the matter is that they are two.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage defines the nature of explicit metaphor (isti'ara musarrah) and presents a key logical dispute regarding its classification. The author first states that the definition of isti'ara is a matter of disagreement between the majority (al-Jumhur) and al-Amidi. The example given involves the case where something is attributed to a person (Zayd) that is actually perceived only by the intellect, expressed through a revealing utterance that clarifies what is hidden in the mind. The majority opinion holds that such an isti'ara must be considered a type of eloquent simile (tashbih baligh), meaning that the metaphor is essentially a compressed comparison. The phrase 'and the matter is that they are two' likely refers to the view that there are two possibilities: either it is tashbih baligh or something else (perhaps the view of al-Amidi). This passage is important because it connects the linguistic art of metaphor to logical classification, showing that even rhetorical figures are subject to systematic categorization.

Key Terms
الاستعارة المصرية
التشبيه البليغ
الجمهور
الآمدي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) It is a separate category unrelated to simile.
C) It is a type of metonymy (majaz mursal).
D) It is a form of implicit metaphor (isti'ara makniyya).

Key Takeaway
The classification of isti'ara is not merely linguistic but a logical issue debated between the majority and al-Amidi, with implications for how metaphors function in argumentation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Three Types of Definitions: Hadd, Rasm, and Lafzī
Author divides definitions into three kinds: hadd, rasm, and lafzī

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three types of definitions (hadd, rasm, lafzi) and identify each type based on its components.

Core Idea
A definition is either complete (hadd), descriptive (rasm), or verbal (lafzī) — each serves a different logical purpose.

Before we use definitions in reasoning, we must understand what kinds there are. The author categorises definitions into three types, each with a distinct structure. This classification helps you evaluate whether a given definition is precise enough for logical work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types
Read the first line of the passage: a definition is divided into hadd, rasmī, and lafzī. Write these three terms.
2
Extract the components for each type
The passage says hadd uses genus and differentia (jins wa faṣl); rasm uses genus and a property (jins wa khāṣṣa); lafzī replaces a word with a more famous synonym. Note these components.
For lafzī, there is no conceptual analysis—just word substitution.
3
Apply the classification to Islamic examples
Given a definition like 'Human is a rational animal', identify it as hadd because it has genus (animal) and differentia (rational). For 'Human is an animal that laughs', it is rasm because laughs is a property.
Use examples from fiqh or kalam to reinforce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ فِي المُعَرِّفَاتِ (٤٠) مُعَرِّفُ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةٍ قُسِمْ: حَدٌ، وَرَسْمِيٌّ، وَلَفْظِيٌّ عُلِم (٤١) فَـ «الحَدُّ» بـ: الجِنْسِ وَفَضْلٍ وَقَعَا وَ(الرَّسْمُ» بـ : الجِنْسِ وَخَاصَةٍ مَعَا (٤٢) وَنَاقِصُ الحَدِّ بِـ : فَصْلِ ، أَوْ مَعَا جِنسٍ بَعيدٍ، لَا قَرِيبٍ وَقَعَا (٤٣) وَنَاقِصُ الرَّسْمِ» بـ: خَاصَةٍ فَقَط أَوْ مَعَ جِنْسِ أَبْعَدٍ قَدِ ارْتَبَط (٤٤) وَمَا بِلَفْظِيّ» لَدَيْهِمْ شُهِرَا : بْدِيلُ لَفْظُ بِرَدِيفٍ أَشْهَرَا
A section on definitions. (40) A definition is divided into three: ḥadd, rasmī, and lafẓī, it is known. (41) The ḥadd is by genus and differentia; and the rasm is by genus and property together. (42) And the incomplete ḥadd is by a differentia alone, or with a remote genus, not a proximate one. (43) And the incomplete rasm is by a property only, or with a more remote genus it is connected. (44) And what is called 'lafẓī' among them is well-known: replacement of a word with a more famous synonym.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a classification of definitions (ta‘rīf) into three types. The first is ḥadd (complete definition), which consists of the proximate genus (jins qarīb) and the differentia (faṣl). For example, defining human as 'rational animal' uses animal as genus and rational as differentia. The second is rasm (description), which uses the genus and a property (khāṣṣa), like 'animal that laughs' for human. Both ḥadd and rasm can be incomplete: nāqiṣ al-ḥadd is when only the differentia is given, or when the differentia is combined with a remote genus instead of a proximate one; nāqiṣ al-rasm is when only the property is given, or when combined with an even more remote genus. The third type is lafẓī (verbal definition), which simply replaces an unfamiliar word with a more common synonym, e.g., defining 'muhannad' as 'sword'.

Key Terms
حد
رسم
لفظي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which definition classifies 'human' as 'animal that walks on two legs'?
A) Ḥadd
B) Rasm
C) Nāqiṣ al-ḥadd
D) Lafzī

Key Takeaway
The three types of definitions—hadd, rasm, and lafzi—correspond to complete, descriptive, and verbal clarifications, each with distinct components.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Classify each definition and state why: (a) 'Wine is an intoxicating beverage' (b) 'Salat is specific acts with takbir and taslim' (c) 'Muhannad means sword'.
?

Incomplete Definitions: Nāqiṣ al-Ḥadd and Nāqiṣ al-Rasm
Author lists incomplete forms of ḥadd and rasm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify incomplete definitions (naqis al-hadd and naqis al-rasm) and explain why they lack logical completeness.

Core Idea
An incomplete definition fails to include both a proximate genus and a differentia, making it logically insufficient.

The same passage that introduced the three types also gives their incomplete versions. Understanding what makes a definition incomplete helps you spot weak definitions in theological and legal arguments.

Guided Path
1
Recall the complete forms
Remember that a complete ḥadd requires proximate genus + differentia; a complete rasm requires genus + property.
2
Find the incomplete versions
The passage says nāqiṣ al-ḥadd is either (i) differentia alone, or (ii) differentia with a remote genus (not proximate). Nāqiṣ al-rasm is either (i) property alone, or (ii) property with a more remote genus.
Remote genus means a higher, less specific category.
3
Assess why each is incomplete
For ḥadd, missing the proximate genus means the definition does not place the thing in its immediate category. For rasm, missing the proximate genus weakens the description.
Example: 'Human is rational' (only differentia) is nāqiṣ al-ḥadd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ فِي المُعَرِّفَاتِ (٤٠) مُعَرِّفُ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةٍ قُسِمْ: حَدٌ، وَرَسْمِيٌّ، وَلَفْظِيٌّ عُلِم (٤١) فَـ «الحَدُّ» بـ: الجِنْسِ وَفَضْلٍ وَقَعَا وَ(الرَّسْمُ» بـ : الجِنْسِ وَخَاصَةٍ مَعَا (٤٢) وَنَاقِصُ الحَدِّ بِـ : فَصْلِ ، أَوْ مَعَا جِنسٍ بَعيدٍ، لَا قَرِيبٍ وَقَعَا (٤٣) وَنَاقِصُ الرَّسْمِ» بـ: خَاصَةٍ فَقَط أَوْ مَعَ جِنْسِ أَبْعَدٍ قَدِ ارْتَبَط (٤٤) وَمَا بِلَفْظِيّ» لَدَيْهِمْ شُهِرَا : بْدِيلُ لَفْظُ بِرَدِيفٍ أَشْهَرَا
A section on definitions. (40) A definition is divided into three: ḥadd, rasmī, and lafẓī, it is known. (41) The ḥadd is by genus and differentia; and the rasm is by genus and property together. (42) And the incomplete ḥadd is by a differentia alone, or with a remote genus, not a proximate one. (43) And the incomplete rasm is by a property only, or with a more remote genus it is connected. (44) And what is called 'lafẓī' among them is well-known: replacement of a word with a more famous synonym.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a classification of definitions (ta‘rīf) into three types. The first is ḥadd (complete definition), which consists of the proximate genus (jins qarīb) and the differentia (faṣl). For example, defining human as 'rational animal' uses animal as genus and rational as differentia. The second is rasm (description), which uses the genus and a property (khāṣṣa), like 'animal that laughs' for human. Both ḥadd and rasm can be incomplete: nāqiṣ al-ḥadd is when only the differentia is given, or when the differentia is combined with a remote genus instead of a proximate one; nāqiṣ al-rasm is when only the property is given, or when combined with an even more remote genus. The third type is lafẓī (verbal definition), which simply replaces an unfamiliar word with a more common synonym, e.g., defining 'muhannad' as 'sword'.

Conditions for a Valid Definition
Author lists eight conditions for a valid definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate whether a definition satisfies all eight conditions required for a valid ḥadd (complete definition).

Core Idea
A valid definition must be coextensive, convertible, clear, non-circular, literal, and unambiguous.

In Islamic logic, a definition (ḥadd) is not just any description; it must meet strict criteria to ensure it precisely captures the essence of the definiendum. The author lists eight conditions that any valid definition must satisfy. These conditions guard against definitions that are too broad, too narrow, circular, metaphorical, ambiguous, or include irrelevant information. Understanding these conditions is essential for constructing reliable definitions in the Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and the definiendum
Locate what is being defined (the term) and the defining expression. This is the first step to apply the conditions.
2
Check coextensiveness (muṭṭarid)
The definition must apply to every individual of the definiendum. If any instance is excluded, the definition is too narrow.
For example, defining 'human' as 'substance' fails because substance includes non-humans.
3
Check conversibility (mun‘akis)
The definition must apply only to the definiendum. The converse must hold: everything that satisfies the definition is an instance of the definiendum.
This ensures the definition is not too broad.
4
Assess clarity (ẓāhir vs. lā ab‘ad)
The definition must be clearer than the definiendum. Avoid terms that are more obscure or remote.
If the definiendum is common and the definition uses technical jargon, it may violate lā ab‘ad.
5
Eliminate circularity (lā musāwī and lā bimā yudrā bi-maḥdūd)
The definition must not be exactly equivalent to the definiendum (circular) nor refer back to the definiendum itself.
Example: 'A tree is a plant that is a tree' is circular.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَشَرْطُ كُلِّ : أَنْ يُرَى «مُطَرِدَا» مُنْعَكِساً»، و«ظَاهِراً» لَا أَبْعَدَا (٤٦) وَلَا مُسَاوِياً»، وَلَا تَجَوُّزَا» بِلَا قَرِينَةٍ بِهَا تُحُرِّزَا (٤٧) وَلَا بِمَا يُدْرَى بِمَحْدُودٍ»، وَلَا مُشْتَرَكِ مِنَ القَرِينَةِ خَلَا» (٤٨) وَعِنْدَهُمْ مِنْ جُمْلَةِ المَرْدُودِ أَنْ تَدْخُلَ الأَحْكَامُ فِي الحُدُودِ (٤٩) وَلَا يَجُوزُ فِي الحُدُودِ ذِكْرُ أَوْ » وَجَائِزٌ فِي الرَّسْمِ فَادْرِ مَا رَوَوْا
And the condition of every [definition] is that it be seen as coextensive (muṭṭarid), conversive (mun‘akis), apparent (ẓāhir), not more remote (lā ab‘ad), (46) and not equal, and not metaphorical without a clue by which one guards against it, (47) and not defined by what is known by the definiendum, and not ambiguous devoid of a clue. (48) And according to them, from the category of rejected is that rulings enter into definitions. (49) And it is not permissible in definitions to mention 'or', and it is permissible in rasm, so understand what they reported.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage lists the conditions that any valid definition (ta‘rīf) must satisfy. There are eight main conditions: (1) muṭṭarid (coextensive): it must apply to all individuals of the definiendum and nothing else. (2) mun‘akis (conversible): it must be true in reverse, e.g., if A is defined as B, then everything that is B is A. (3) ẓāhir (apparent): the definition must be clearer than the definiendum. (4) lā ab‘ad (not more remote): the terms should not be more obscure than the definiendum. (5) lā musāwi (not equal): the definition should not be exactly equivalent to the definiendum (circular). (6) lā tajawwuz (not metaphorical): it should not be figurative without a clarifying clue (qarīna). (7) lā bimā yudrā bi-maḥdūd (not defined by what the definiendum defines): no circularity. (8) lā mushtarak (not ambiguous): it should not be a homonym without a clue. Additionally, the author mentions that definitions should not include rulings (aḥkām), e.g., 'wine is forbidden' is not a definition. Also, the word 'or' (aw) is forbidden in ḥadd but allowed in rasm, because rasm allows for alternative properties.

Key Terms
مطرد
منعكس
ظاهر
لا أبعد
لا مساو
لا تجوز
لا مشترك
أو

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Muṭṭarid
B) Mun‘akis
C) Ẓāhir
D) Lā ab‘ad

Key Takeaway
A valid definition in Islamic logic must be coextensive, convertible, clear, non-circular, literal, and free from rulings and disjunctions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take the definition of 'wudhu' (ablution) as: 'washing the face and hands and wiping the head and feet with water with intention.' Check whether it satisfies muṭṭarid and mun‘akis. Does it apply to all types of wudhu? Does it exclude other acts?
?
Identify which condition is violated by the definition: 'Salat is the act of worship that is obligatory for every Muslim.' (Hint: it includes a ruling).

Definition and Derivation of 'Basmala'
Bajuri defines 'basmala' as a verbal noun from 'basmala', explains its derivation via 'naht', and discusses its usage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the derivation of 'basmala' via naht and distinguish between its literal and metaphorical uses based on al-Bajuri's commentary.

Core Idea
The word 'basmala' is a blend (naht) of 'Bismillah', showing how Arabic condenses key phrases into single verbs.

In this passage from his hashya on al-Bannani's commentary, al-Bajuri unpacks the term 'basmala' — the first word in many Islamic texts. He explains not only its meaning but also the linguistic process behind its formation. Understanding this helps you see how later scholars adapted language for precise expression.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum and its lexical class
Find what is being defined: the word 'basmala'. Al-Bajuri identifies it as a verbal noun (masdar) derived from the verb 'basmala'. This is a regular derivation pattern in Arabic, like 'dahraja' from 'al-hamdu lillah'.
2
Trace the derivation process: naht
Understand that 'basmala' is formed by blending letters from 'Bismillah' through a process called naht. Note the conditions: it is not required to preserve the entire first word, nor to take from all words, nor to match voweling, but the order of letters is important.
The example of 'talbaq' from 'Atala Allah baqa'aka' illustrates the order condition.
3
Analyze the metaphorical extension
The verbal noun is used metaphorically to refer to the actual phrase 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim'. This is a majaz (metaphor) where the verbal noun stands for the object. Later, it became a haqiqa 'urfiyya (customary literal term).
This shift is common in Islamic terminology.
4
Evaluate the types of naht
Al-Bajuri notes that naht is usually samai' (based on transmitted usage) according to al-Shumunni, but Ibn Faris considered it qiyasi (regular by analogy). Reflect on how this affects our understanding of word formation in Arabic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ابْتَدَأَ بِالبَسْمَلَةِ) مصدرٌ قياسي لـ «بَسْمَلَ» ـ كـ: «دَحْرَجَ ، دَحْرَجَةٌ» ـ إذا قال : «بسم الله» على ما في «الصحاح» ، أو إذا كتبها على ما في تهذيب الأَزْهَرِيِّ ، فهي بمعنى القول أو الكتابة، لكن أطلقوها على نفس بسم الله الرَّحمن الرّحيم» مجازاً، من إطلاق المصدر على المفعول؛ لعلاقة اللُّزوم، ثم صارت حقيقة عرفية. وهي من باب النحت وهو : أن يختصر من كلمتين فأكثر كلمةً واحدةً : - ولا يُشترط فيه حفظ الكلمة الأولى بتمامها بالاستقراء، خلافاً لبعضهم. ولا الأخذ من كل الكلمات. - ولا موافقة الحركات والسكنات؛ كما يُعلم من شواهده. نعم ؛ يُفهم من كلامهم اعتبار ترتيب الحروف، ولذا عُدَّ ما وقع للشَّهاب الخَفَاجِيِّ في شفاء الغليل من «طبلق» ـ بتقديم الباء على اللام - إذا قال: «أطال الله بقاءك» سَبْقُ قلم، والقياسُ «طلبق». والنَّحتُ مع كثرته في كلام العرب سماعي ، كما صرح به الشُّمُنِّي، ونقل عن اللغة لابن فارس قياسيّته. ثمَّ مُرادُهُ : أنَّه ابتدأ بالبسملة نطقاً وكتابة أمَّا الثَّاني فدليله : المشاهدة، وأمَّا الأَوَّل فدليلُهُ : أَنَّ مَن كتب شيئاً تلفظ به غالباً .
('He began with the basmala') is a regular verbal noun from 'basmala' — like 'dahraja, dahrajatun' — when he says 'Bismillah' according to what is in al-Sihah, or when he writes it according to what is in Tahdhib al-Azhari. So it (basmala) means speaking or writing. However, they (the scholars) applied it (the verbal noun) metaphorically to the phrase itself 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' as a metaphor, by using the verbal noun for the object (i.e., the phrase), due to the relation of implication. Then it became a customarily literal term. It (the derivation) is of the category of 'naht' (blending), which is: to shorten from two or more words into one word. It is not a condition that the first word be preserved in its entirety according to induction, contrary to some. Nor is it a condition to take from all the words. Nor is it a condition to match the voweling and consonantal signs (harakat and sukunat), as is known from its examples. Rather, it is understood from their speech that the order of letters is considered, and thus what occurred to al-Shihab al-Khafaji in Shifa' al-Ghalil of 'tiblaq' — with the ba' before the lam — when he said 'Atala Allah baqa'aka' is a slip of the pen, and the analogue is 'talbaq'. And naht, despite its abundance in Arab speech, is based on hearing (samai'), as al-Shumunni stated, and it is transmitted from Ibn Faris in al-Lugha that it is qiyasi (regular by analogy). Then his meaning is: he began with the basmala in speech and writing. As for the second (writing), its evidence is direct observation; as for the first (speech), its evidence is that whoever writes something usually utters it.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and explanatory note from al-Bajuri's hashya on the opening phrase 'He began with the basmala' from the commentary on al-Sullam. He explains that 'basmala' is a verbal noun (masdar) derived regularly from the verb 'basmala', which means to say or write 'Bismillah'. This is analogous to 'dahraja' meaning to say or write 'al-hamdu lillah'. The term 'basmala' itself is a metaphorical extension (majaz) from the verbal noun to the actual utterance, later becoming a customary literal term (haqiqa 'urfiyya). He then discusses the linguistic concept of 'naht' (blending), where multiple words are compressed into a single word, akin to 'basmala' from 'Bismillah'. He outlines the conditions (or lack thereof) for naht: it is not required to preserve the entire first word, nor to take letters from every word, nor to match harakat and sukunat. However, the order of letters must be preserved, giving an example of a slip where a scholar mistakenly wrote 'tiblaq' instead of 'talbaq' for 'Atala Allah baqa'aka'. He notes that naht is primarily samai' (based on transmitted usage), but Ibn Faris considered it qiyasi (regular by analogy). Finally, he clarifies that the author's intent in 'he began with the basmala' covers both spoken and written commencement, with evidence for writing being direct observation and for speech being the general habit of uttering what one writes.

النحت

The term 'basmala' is derived via naht from 'Bismillah', and its usage shifted from a verbal noun to a customary literal term for the phrase itself.

The Specific Meaning of the Basmala as a Specificity of This Ummah
Defines what is meant by the basmala being a specificity of this ummah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the precise meaning of 'al-mukhtaṣṣ' in this context and explain why the Arabic basmala in its known order is unique to the Islamic ummah.

Core Idea
The Arabic basmala in its known order is what is unique to this ummah, not just any basmala.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies an important nuance: when scholars say the basmala is a specificity of the Islamic ummah, they mean specifically the Arabic wording in the well-known order. This refinement is crucial for understanding how the basmala of previous scriptures relates to the Islamic tradition. Let's break down the logical steps of this definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Find 'المختص' in the Arabic. What is it that is claimed to be specific?
It is what is attributed uniquely to this ummah.
2
Extract the defining characteristics
What are the two limiting conditions: language (Arabic) and order (this arrangement)?
The commentator states 'اللفظ العربي على هذا الترتيب'.
3
Consider the objection from previous scriptures
The commentator raises a potential objection: what about the basmala in other revealed books? How does he handle it?
He gives two possibilities: different order or non-Arabic.
4
Analyze the resolution
The resolution is that the Arabic basmala that continues to be Arabic (i.e., preserved) is what is unique. Understand the distinction.
The phrase 'المستمر عربيته' is key.
5
Test the definition's completeness
Does this definition exclude all non-Islamic basmalas? Does it include only the Islamic one?
It includes the Islamic basmala and excludes others.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالمُخْتَصُّ بِهَذِهِ الأُمَّةِ إِنَّمَا هُوَ اللَّفْظُ العَرِبِيُّ عَلَى هَذَا التَّرْتِيبِ، وَعَلَى هَذَا يُحْمَلُ قَوْلُ مَنْ قَالَ: بِأَنَّهَا مِنْ خُصُوصِيَّاتِ هَذِهِ الأُمَّةِ. وَعَمَلًا بِخَبَرِ: كُلُّ أَمْرٍ ذِي بَالٍ لَا يُبْدَأُ فِيْهِ بِ: بِسْمِ اللهِ الرَّحْمَنِ الرَّحِيمِ، فَهُوَ أَبْتَرُ أَوْ: «أَجْذَمُ» أَوْ: «أَقْطَعُ» رِوَايَات. ثُمَّ إِنْ كَانَ المُرَادُ: أَنَّ بَسْمَلَةَ بَقِيَّةِ الكُتُبِ نَزَلَتْ عَرَبِيَّةً إِلَّا أَنَّهَا عَلَى غَيْرِ هَذَا التَّرْتِيبِ، كَانَ الأَمْرُ ظَاهِرًا. وَإِنْ كَانَ المُرَادُ أَنَّهَا نَزَلَتْ غَيْرَ عَرَبِيَّةٍ كَانَ مُخَالِفًا لِمَا وَرَدَ مِنْ: أَنَّ كُلَّ كِتَابٍ نَزَلَ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ فَهُوَ عَرَبِيٌّ، إِلَّا أَنَّ كُلَّ نَبِيٍّ عَبَّرَ عَنْهُ بِلِسَانِ قَوْمِهِ. إِلَّا أَنْ يُجَابَ بِأَنَّ قَوْلَهُ: وَالمُخْتَصُّ بِهَذِهِ الأُمَّةِ إِنَّمَا هُوَ اللَّفْظُ العَرَبِيُّ... إِلَخ، مَعْنَاهُ: العَرَبِيُّ المُسْتَمِرُّ عَرَبِيَّتَهُ، فَتَدَبَّر. قَوْلُهُ: (وَعَمَلًا) إِنَّمَا عَبَّرَ بِـ «العَمَلِ» هُنَا، وَثَمَّ بِـ «الاقْتِدَاءِ»؛ لِتَضَمُّنِ الخَبَرِ الأَمْرَ، بِخِلَافِ القُرْآنِ، فَإِنَّهُ لَمْ يَتَضَمَّنْهُ كَتَضَمُّنِ الخَبَرِ. قَوْلُهُ: «لَا يُبْدَأُ» صِفَةٌ ثَانِيَةٌ لِـ «أَمْرِ» مِنْ بَابِ النَّعْتِ بِالجُمْلَةِ أَحْسَنُ مِنْ عَكْسِهِ النَّعْتِ بِالمُفْرَدِ، وَهُوَ بَعْدُ أَحْسَنُ. قَوْلُهُ: («فِيهِ) أَيْ: بِسَبَبِهِ. وَفَائِدَةُ الإِتْيَانِ بِـ «فِي» الدَّالَّةِ عَلَى السَّبَبِيَّةِ مَعَ صِحَّةِ تَرْكِهَا: إِفَادَةُ أَنَّ المَطْلُوبَ كَوْنُ الأَمْرِ ذِي البَالِ سَبَبًا بَاعِثًا عَلَى التَّسْمِيَةِ فِي ابْتِدَائِهِ، لَا مُطْلَقُ وُقُوعِ التَّسْمِيَةِ فِي ابْتِدَائِهِ وَلَوْ بِسَبَبٍ آخَرَ؛ بِحَيْثُ يَكُونَ هُوَ غَيْرَ مَنْظُورٍ إِلَيْهِ عِنْدَ التَّسْمِيَةِ.
And what is specific to this nation is only the Arabic expression in this arrangement. And upon this is carried the statement of whoever said: that it is from the specificities of this nation. And acting upon the report: 'Every matter of importance that is not begun in it with Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim, then it is curtailed' or 'mutilated' or 'amputated' – narrations. Then if what is meant is that the basmala of the other books descended as Arabic except that it is not in this arrangement, then the matter is apparent. And if what is meant is that it descended as non-Arabic, it contradicts what is narrated: that every book that descended from heaven is Arabic, except that every prophet expressed it in the language of his people. Unless it is answered that his saying: 'And what is specific to this nation is only the Arabic expression... etc.' means: the Arabic that continues in its Arabicness, so consider. His saying: 'and acting' – He only expressed with 'act' here, and there with 'following' because the report contains an implicit command, unlike the Quran, for it does not contain it like the report does. His saying: 'is not begun' – a second adjective for 'matter' from the category of adjectival clause, which is better than the opposite of adjectival with a single word, and it is even better. His saying: 'in it' – i.e., by it. And the benefit of bringing 'in' which indicates causality, even though it is correct to omit it, is to indicate that what is required is that the matter of importance is a cause motivating the naming in its beginning, not the absolute occurrence of the naming in its beginning even if by another cause, such that it is not regarded at the time of naming.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage expands on the point that the basmala in its specific Arabic wording is unique to the Islamic ummah. The commentator explains that when some say the basmala is a specificity of this ummah, they mean the Arabic phrase in this order. He then discusses the hadith that commands beginning important matters with basmala, noting the textual variants (abtar, ajzham, aqta'). He addresses a potential objection: what about the basmala in previous scriptures? He explains that if those basmalas were Arabic but in a different order, it's fine; if they were non-Arabic, that contradicts the principle that all revealed books are Arabic. The resolution is that the Arabic basmala that continues to be Arabic (i.e., preserved in Arabic) is what is specific. Then he analyzes the word 'acting' versus 'following' in context, and the grammatical structure of 'la yubda'u'. The benefit of the preposition 'fi' indicating causation is explained to ensure that the basmala is directly related to the importance of the matter, not just any naming.

بسملة
أبتر/أجذم/أقطع

Key Takeaway
The basmala's uniqueness to the Islamic ummah is not about the concept of beginning with God's name, but specifically the Arabic phrase 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' in its fixed order.

The Hadith on Beginning with Basmala and Its Grammatical Nuances
Analyzes the grammatical and causative nuances of the hadith on beginning with basmala.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the grammatical structure of the hadith 'كل أمر ذي بال لا يبدأ فيه ببسم الله...' and explain the significance of the preposition 'في' and the adjectival clause.

Core Idea
The hadith emphasizes that the basmala is a causal result of the matter's importance, not just any timing.

The commentator dives into the grammatical nuances of the hadith that commands beginning important matters with basmala. He explains why the phrase 'la yubda'u fihi' is used and the implication of the preposition 'fi' indicating causation. This shows how precise language affects the understanding of prophetic guidance.

Guided Path
1
Locate the hadith text in the passage
Identify the phrase: 'كل أمر ذي بال لا يبدأ فيه ببسم الله الرحمن الرحيم فهو أبتر' and its variants.
The hadith appears in full in the earlier part of the source text.
2
Analyze the grammatical structure of 'لا يبدأ'
The commentator notes it is a second adjective for 'amr' (matter) using a clause, which is more effective than a single word adjective.
This is from the category of 'na't bil-jumla' (adjectival clause).
3
Examine the preposition 'في'
Why is 'fi' used? It normally means 'in', but here it indicates causality (sababiyya). Understand how 'fi' can signify cause.
The commentator explicitly says 'ay: bi-sababihi' (i.e., by it).
4
Understand the benefit of 'fi' with causality
The implication: the matter itself should be the reason for reciting basmala, not just that basmala happens to be said at the start for some other reason.
The benefit is to ensure that the naming (basmala) is motivated by the importance of the matter.
5
Compare with the Quranic context
The commentator contrasts 'amal' (action/acting) used here with 'iqtida' (following) used elsewhere, because the hadith contains an implicit command unlike the Quran.
This shows sensitivity to textual context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالمُخْتَصُّ بِهَذِهِ الأُمَّةِ إِنَّمَا هُوَ اللَّفْظُ العَرِبِيُّ عَلَى هَذَا التَّرْتِيبِ، وَعَلَى هَذَا يُحْمَلُ قَوْلُ مَنْ قَالَ: بِأَنَّهَا مِنْ خُصُوصِيَّاتِ هَذِهِ الأُمَّةِ. وَعَمَلًا بِخَبَرِ: كُلُّ أَمْرٍ ذِي بَالٍ لَا يُبْدَأُ فِيْهِ بِ: بِسْمِ اللهِ الرَّحْمَنِ الرَّحِيمِ، فَهُوَ أَبْتَرُ أَوْ: «أَجْذَمُ» أَوْ: «أَقْطَعُ» رِوَايَات. ثُمَّ إِنْ كَانَ المُرَادُ: أَنَّ بَسْمَلَةَ بَقِيَّةِ الكُتُبِ نَزَلَتْ عَرَبِيَّةً إِلَّا أَنَّهَا عَلَى غَيْرِ هَذَا التَّرْتِيبِ، كَانَ الأَمْرُ ظَاهِرًا. وَإِنْ كَانَ المُرَادُ أَنَّهَا نَزَلَتْ غَيْرَ عَرَبِيَّةٍ كَانَ مُخَالِفًا لِمَا وَرَدَ مِنْ: أَنَّ كُلَّ كِتَابٍ نَزَلَ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ فَهُوَ عَرَبِيٌّ، إِلَّا أَنَّ كُلَّ نَبِيٍّ عَبَّرَ عَنْهُ بِلِسَانِ قَوْمِهِ. إِلَّا أَنْ يُجَابَ بِأَنَّ قَوْلَهُ: وَالمُخْتَصُّ بِهَذِهِ الأُمَّةِ إِنَّمَا هُوَ اللَّفْظُ العَرَبِيُّ... إِلَخ، مَعْنَاهُ: العَرَبِيُّ المُسْتَمِرُّ عَرَبِيَّتَهُ، فَتَدَبَّر. قَوْلُهُ: (وَعَمَلًا) إِنَّمَا عَبَّرَ بِـ «العَمَلِ» هُنَا، وَثَمَّ بِـ «الاقْتِدَاءِ»؛ لِتَضَمُّنِ الخَبَرِ الأَمْرَ، بِخِلَافِ القُرْآنِ، فَإِنَّهُ لَمْ يَتَضَمَّنْهُ كَتَضَمُّنِ الخَبَرِ. قَوْلُهُ: «لَا يُبْدَأُ» صِفَةٌ ثَانِيَةٌ لِـ «أَمْرِ» مِنْ بَابِ النَّعْتِ بِالجُمْلَةِ أَحْسَنُ مِنْ عَكْسِهِ النَّعْتِ بِالمُفْرَدِ، وَهُوَ بَعْدُ أَحْسَنُ. قَوْلُهُ: («فِيهِ) أَيْ: بِسَبَبِهِ. وَفَائِدَةُ الإِتْيَانِ بِـ «فِي» الدَّالَّةِ عَلَى السَّبَبِيَّةِ مَعَ صِحَّةِ تَرْكِهَا: إِفَادَةُ أَنَّ المَطْلُوبَ كَوْنُ الأَمْرِ ذِي البَالِ سَبَبًا بَاعِثًا عَلَى التَّسْمِيَةِ فِي ابْتِدَائِهِ، لَا مُطْلَقُ وُقُوعِ التَّسْمِيَةِ فِي ابْتِدَائِهِ وَلَوْ بِسَبَبٍ آخَرَ؛ بِحَيْثُ يَكُونَ هُوَ غَيْرَ مَنْظُورٍ إِلَيْهِ عِنْدَ التَّسْمِيَةِ.
And what is specific to this nation is only the Arabic expression in this arrangement. And upon this is carried the statement of whoever said: that it is from the specificities of this nation. And acting upon the report: 'Every matter of importance that is not begun in it with Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim, then it is curtailed' or 'mutilated' or 'amputated' – narrations. Then if what is meant is that the basmala of the other books descended as Arabic except that it is not in this arrangement, then the matter is apparent. And if what is meant is that it descended as non-Arabic, it contradicts what is narrated: that every book that descended from heaven is Arabic, except that every prophet expressed it in the language of his people. Unless it is answered that his saying: 'And what is specific to this nation is only the Arabic expression... etc.' means: the Arabic that continues in its Arabicness, so consider. His saying: 'and acting' – He only expressed with 'act' here, and there with 'following' because the report contains an implicit command, unlike the Quran, for it does not contain it like the report does. His saying: 'is not begun' – a second adjective for 'matter' from the category of adjectival clause, which is better than the opposite of adjectival with a single word, and it is even better. His saying: 'in it' – i.e., by it. And the benefit of bringing 'in' which indicates causality, even though it is correct to omit it, is to indicate that what is required is that the matter of importance is a cause motivating the naming in its beginning, not the absolute occurrence of the naming in its beginning even if by another cause, such that it is not regarded at the time of naming.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage expands on the point that the basmala in its specific Arabic wording is unique to the Islamic ummah. The commentator explains that when some say the basmala is a specificity of this ummah, they mean the Arabic phrase in this order. He then discusses the hadith that commands beginning important matters with basmala, noting the textual variants (abtar, ajzham, aqta'). He addresses a potential objection: what about the basmala in previous scriptures? He explains that if those basmalas were Arabic but in a different order, it's fine; if they were non-Arabic, that contradicts the principle that all revealed books are Arabic. The resolution is that the Arabic basmala that continues to be Arabic (i.e., preserved in Arabic) is what is specific. Then he analyzes the word 'acting' versus 'following' in context, and the grammatical structure of 'la yubda'u'. The benefit of the preposition 'fi' indicating causation is explained to ensure that the basmala is directly related to the importance of the matter, not just any naming.

Key Terms
عمل
اقتداء
فيه (بسببه)
صفة بالجملة
نعت بالمفرد

Key Takeaway
The hadith teaches that the basmala should be recited because the matter is important, not just as a routine, and the grammar of the hadith reinforces this causal connection.

Rhetorical Analysis: Tashbih Baligh vs. Isti'ara in a Hadith
Analyzes the rhetorical form of the hadith ending, classifying it as tashbih baligh or isti'ara with discussion of the dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify an Arabic expression as tashbih baligh or isti'ara musarrahah, and explain the morphological and rhetorical basis for the hadith's description using physical defects to convey moral deficiency.

Core Idea
A physical curtailed tail becomes a metaphor for spiritual incompleteness.

This lesson delves into the commentator's analysis of a hadith that uses words like 'abtar' (curtailed) to describe a deficient act. We'll explore the rhetorical dispute over whether it's a simile or metaphor, and how physical terms are applied to moral concepts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rhetorical categories
The passage discusses two possibilities: tashbih baligh (eloquent simile) and isti'ara musarrahah (explicit metaphor). Note the definition of each.
Tashbih baligh omits both tool and aspect; isti'ara does not combine both sides.
2
Define tashbih baligh
Tashbih baligh is defined as a simile where the tool (like 'as') and the aspect of resemblance are omitted. The phrase 'fahuwa abtar' means 'he is like one curtailed'. Confirm that both elements are absent here.
In the hadith, the tool (ka-) and aspect (absolute deficiency) are omitted, fitting tashbih baligh.
3
Analyze the dispute
The majority holds that 'Zayd is a lion' is tashbih baligh, not isti'ara, because metaphor does not combine both sides of the comparison. Al-Sa'd disagrees. How does this apply to our hadith?
The hadith phrase similarly combines 'matter' and 'curtailed', so the majority would classify it as tashbih baligh.
4
Examine the adjectives
'Abtar', 'ajzham', 'aqta' are forms of adjective derived from intransitive verbs. Their literal meaning is physical, but the aspect of resemblance is absolute deficiency, both physical and moral.
The commentator notes they are derived from intransitive verbs with broken middle letter, making the af'al pattern regular.
5
Apply the moral deficiency concept
The commentator gives examples: a composition with little benefit, eating without nourishment, reading with distraction. These show how a physical term conveys a moral lack.
Moral deficiency is expressed as physical defect, a common rhetorical device in the Islamic tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْكَلَامُ عَلَى كُلِّ: مِنْ بَابِ التَّشْبِيهِ البَلِيغِ - وَهُوَ: «مَا حُذِفَ فِيهِ أَدَاةُ التَّشْبِيهِ وَوَجْهُ الشَّبَهِ، وَالمَعْنَى: فَهُوَ كَالأَبْتَرِ» - الَّذِي هُوَ: مَقْطُوعُ الذَّنَبِ، أَوْ كَالأَجْذَمِ» - الَّذِي هُوَ مَنْ ذَهَبَتْ أَنَامِلُهُ مِنَ الجُذَامِ، - أَوْ كَالأَقْطَع» - الَّذِي هُوَ: مَقْطُوعُ اليَدِ، وَعَلى كُلِّ فَوَجْهُ الشَّبَهِ: مُطْلَقُ النَّقْصِ، وَإِنْ كَانَ فِي المُشَبَّهِ بِهِ حِسّيًّا، وَفِي المُشَبَّهِ مَعْنَوِيًّا. أَوْ مِنْ بَابِ الاِسْتِعَارَةِ المُصَرَّحَةِ عَلَى الخِلافِ بَيْنَ الجُمْهُورِ وَالسَّعْدِ فِي نَحْوِ: زَيْدُ أَسَدٌ»؛ حَيْثُ قَالَ الجُمْهُورُ: يَجِبُ أَنْ يَكُونَ مِنْ بَابِ التَّشْبِيهِ البَلِيعْ، وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَكُونَ مِنْ بَابِ الاسْتِعَارَةِ؛ لأَنَّهُ لَا يُجْمَعُ فِيهَا بَيْنَ طَرَفَيِ التَّشْبِيهِ - أَعْني: المُشَبَّهَ وَالمُشَبَّهَ بِهِ... ثُمَّ إِنَّ «أَجْدَمَ» و«أَبْتَرَ» و«أَقْطَعَ»: صِفَاتٌ مُشَبَّهَةٌ مَصُوغَةٌ مِنْ أَفْعَالٍ لَازِمَةٍ مَكْسُورَةِ العَيْنِ؛ لِيَكُونَ صَوْغُ الصِّفَةِ المُشَبَّهَةِ الَّتِي عَلَى «أَفْعَلَ» مِنْهَا قِيَاسًا. قَوْلُهُ: (وَفِي المُشَبَّهِ مَعْنَوِيًّا) أَيْ: وَإِنْ تَمَّ حَسًّا، وَالنَّقْصُ المَعْنَوِيُّ: فِي نَحْوِ التَّأْلِيفِ: قِلَّةُ انْتِفَاعِ النَّاسِ بِهِ وَقِلَّةُ الثَّوَابِ عَلَيْهِ. وَفِي نَحْوِ الأَكْلِ: قِلَّةُ انْتِفَاعِ الجِسْمِ بِهِ. وَفِي نَحْوِ القِرَاءَةِ: قِلَّةُ انْتِفَاعِ القَارِئِ بِهَا؛ لِوَسْوَسَةِ الشَّيْطَانِ حِينَئِذٍ.
And the discussion concerning each: from the category of eloquent simile – which is: 'that in which the tool of simile and the aspect of resemblance are omitted, and the meaning is: so it is like the curtailed' – which is: cut off from the tail, or 'like the mutilated' – which is: one whose fingers have gone from leprosy, or 'like the amputated' – which is: one whose hand is cut off. And in each case, the aspect of resemblance is absolute deficiency, even if it is physical in the resembled thing and moral in the thing being resembled. Or from the category of explicit metaphor, according to the disagreement between the majority and al-Sa'd concerning examples like: 'Zayd is a lion'; where the majority said: it must be from the category of eloquent simile, and it is not permissible for it to be from the category of metaphor, because in metaphor the two sides of the simile – i.e., the resembled and the resembling – are not combined. Then indeed, 'ajdham', 'abtar', and 'aqta' are adjective forms derived from intransitive verbs with broken middle letter, so that the derivation of the adjective form on the pattern 'af'al' from them is regular. His saying: ('and in the resembled thing moral') – i.e., even if it is physically realized, and moral deficiency: in the case of composition: little benefit of people from it and little reward upon it. In the case of eating: little benefit of the body from it. In the case of reading: little benefit of the reader from it due to the whispering of Satan at that time.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage discusses the rhetorical classification of the hadith's wording 'fahuwa abtar/ajzham/aqta'. The commentator considers whether this is an example of eloquent simile (tashbih baligh) or explicit metaphor (isti'ara musarrahah). He explains that in tashbih baligh, the tool of comparison and the aspect of resemblance are omitted, so the statement 'fahuwa abtar' means 'it is like a curtailed thing'. The aspect of resemblance is 'absolute deficiency', and he notes that in the simile, the deficiency is physical (in the original word meaning) but moral in the target (the matter). Then he introduces a disagreement between the majority of scholars and al-Sa'd al-Taftazani regarding phrases like 'Zayd is a lion': the majority insist it is tashbih baligh, not isti'ara, because isti'ara does not combine both sides of the simile (the subject and the image). Al-Sa'd disagreed. The commentator also discusses the morphological derivation of the words, emphasizing they are derived from intransitive verbs. Finally, he provides examples of moral deficiency: in authorship, eating, and reading – showing that the deficiency is not physical but in benefit or reward.

Key Terms
التشبيه البليغ
الاستعارة المصَّرَّحة
وجه الشبه

Key Takeaway

Four Logical Interpretations of the Basmala
Author lists four possible interpretations of the basmala and discusses their ordering

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four logical interpretations of the basmala based on the quantification of the subject and order them by closeness.

Core Idea
The basmala admits multiple logical forms; the covenant interpretation is the closest.

In this passage, al-Bajuri expands on al-Bannani's commentary to explore the logical quantification of the subject in the basmala. By understanding the four possibilities—covenant, all-inclusive, genus within some, and indefinite—you will see how Islamic logic systematically analyzes even the most fundamental phrases. The ordering reflects which interpretation is considered most probable in the context.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two axes of interpretation
Notice that the possibilities arise from two perspectives: the meaning of the preposition 'ba' (original vs. extra) and the annexation (idafa) of the name. The well-known view treats 'ba' as original, while the opposite treats it as extra.
Both axes yield the same four possibilities, so the focus is on the quantification of the subject.
2
Understand the four quantification categories
The categories are: (1) covenant (al-'ahd) – indicating a specific known entity; (2) all-inclusiveness (al-isti'ghraq) – covering all individuals; (3) genus within some (al-jins fi dhimn al-ba'd) – referring to some individuals generically; (4) indefinite (al-qadiyya al-muhmala) – universal but left unquantified.
These correspond to the four possible interpretations of the basmala: 'the name of Allah' as a specific name, all names, some names, or any name.
3
Note the ordering of closeness
The text states that the first (covenant) is closest, then the second (all-inclusive), then the third (genus within some), then the fourth (indefinite). This ordering is based on how directly each interpretation matches the common understanding of the basmala.
The ordering is not arbitrary; it reflects logical priority.
4
Understand the rebuttal to an objection
An objection is raised: the judgment (beginning) is on the subject, not the object of the preposition. The reply is that the object is subject in meaning, as grammarians confirm. The estimation is 'The name of Allah is begun with.'
This shows how logical analysis interacts with grammatical structure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قدر نحو: «يبتدئ المؤمن بقطع النظر عن الكلية والجزئية كانت: «قضية مهملة»؛ لأن المحكوم عليه فيها كلي، وقد أهمل عن اعتبار الكلية والجزئية، كما هو ضابط القضية المهملة. وكما يصح اعتبار هذه الاحتمالات باعتبار المتعلق؛ بناء على المشهور من أن «الباء» حرف جر أصلي، يصح اعتبارها باعتبار إضافة الاسم إلى «لفظ الجلالة»؛ بناء على مقابل المشهور من أن الباء حرف جر زائد: فإن جعلت للعهد فالأول . وإن جعلت للاستغراق فالثاني . وإن جعلت للجنس في ضمن البعض فالثالث . وإن جعلت في ضمن الأفراد من غير نظر لكلية أو جزئية فالرابع. فإن قيل: كيف يصح هذا مع أن المدار في هذه القضايا على الموضوع، لا على المجرور؟ أجيب بأنه وإن كان مجروراً لفظاً موضوع معنى، ولذا قال التحاة: المجرور مخبر عنه في المعنى؛ والتقدير هنا: اسم الله تعالى مبدوء به. ولا يخفى أن بعض هذه الاحتمالات أقرب من بعض. قال الأنبابي: قوله: (أقرب من بعض) فأولها أقرب، ويليه الثاني، ثم الثالث، ثم الرابع؛ كذا قيل.
And if it is estimated similar to: 'The believer begins by disregarding universality and particularity,' it would be an indefinite proposition (qadiyya muhmala), because that which is judged upon in it is universal, and it has been left indefinite regarding consideration of universality and particularity, as is the rule of the indefinite proposition. And just as it is valid to consider these possibilities with regard to the dependent (muta'allaq), based on the well-known view that the letter 'ba' is an original preposition, it is also valid to consider them with regard to the annexation (idafa) of the noun to the word of Majesty (Lafz al-Jalalah), based on the opposite of the well-known view that the letter 'ba' is an extra preposition. If it is made for covenant (al-'ahd), then the first [possibility]. If it is made for all-inclusiveness (al-isti'ghraq), then the second. If it is made for the genus within some individuals (al-jins fi dhimn al-ba'd), then the third. If it is made for within individuals without regard to universality or particularity, then the fourth. If it is said: How can this be valid while the focus in these propositions is on the subject, not on the object of the preposition? The answer is that it is, even though it is an object in wording, it is a subject in meaning. That is why the grammarians said: 'The object of a preposition is, in meaning, something predicated about.' And the estimation here is: 'The name of Allah, the Exalted, is begun with.' And it is not hidden that some of these possibilities are closer than others. Al-Anbabi said: 'His statement: (closer than others) so the first of them is the closest, then the second, then the third, then the fourth; thus it is said.'
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the possible logical interpretations of the basmala (the phrase 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim') based on the meaning of the preposition 'ba' and the annexation. The author first notes that if the phrase 'the believer begins disregarding universality and particularity' is taken, it becomes an indefinite proposition because the subject is universal but not quantified. Then he explains that the possibilities arise from two axes: the dependent (muta'allaq) and the annexation (idafa). The well-known view treats 'ba' as an original preposition, while the opposite view treats it as extra. For each, we can consider the 'ba' as indicating 'covenant' (known specific one), 'all-inclusiveness' (every believer), 'genus within some' (some believers generically), or 'within individuals without universal/particular' (indefinite). The first is the closest, then second, third, fourth. He then addresses an objection: the judgment is on the subject, not the object. The reply: the object is subject in meaning, as grammarians say. Thus the interpretation is valid. This lesson uses Islamic logic to analyze a fundamental Islamic phrase.

Key Terms
القضية المهملة
العهد
الاستغراق
الجنس في ضمن البعض

The Natural Proposition and Its Inapplicability to the Basmala
Author defines the natural proposition and argues the basmala cannot be of this type

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the natural proposition and determine whether any given proposition qualifies as natural, using the basmala as a test case.

Core Idea
The natural proposition judges essences, not individuals; the basmala cannot be natural because beginning requires an individual agent.

In this passage, the author introduces a new type of proposition: the natural proposition. This is a judgment about the essence or nature of something, ignoring individuals. The basmala, which involves a specific believer beginning with the name of Allah, cannot be a natural proposition because it necessarily refers to individual actions. We will explore the definition, an important correction to the standard example, and the reasoning that excludes the basmala.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of natural proposition
Read the definition: a judgment made upon the genus and nature, disregarding individuals. This means the proposition is about the essence, not about any particular instance.
The Arabic term is 'al-qadiyya al-tabi'iyya'.
2
Examine the first example and its critique
The example given is 'Man is better than woman.' But the author (through al-Anbabi) notes that this is a poor example because 'goodness' (khairiyya) is only meaningful when comparing individuals. A better example would be 'Man is a rational animal' or 'Man is a species,' which describe the nature without comparison.
The critique shows that the example must define the essence, not imply superiority.
3
Apply the definition to the basmala
Consider the basmala: 'In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful.' Could it be a natural proposition? The author argues no, because the phrase refers to a specific believer performing the act of beginning, and the name of Allah is used as an instrument. Neither the believer nor the name can be taken as a mere genus or nature; they are concrete individuals.
The basmala is an action-based utterance, not a statement about essences.

بَقِيَ مِنْ أَقْسَامِ القَضَايَا : القَضِيَّةُ الطَّبِيعِيَّةُ ، وَهِيَ : مَا حُكِمَ فِيهَا عَلَى الجِنْسِ وَالطَّبِيعَةِ، بِقَطْعِ النَّظَرِ عَنِ الأَفْرَادِ» ؛ كَأَنْ تَقُولَ: «الرَّجُلُ خَيْرٌ مِنَ المَرْأَةِ» ، فَإِنَّ المُرَادَ : أَنَّ جِنْسَ الرَّجُلِ وَطَبِيعَتَهُ خَيْرٌ مِنْ جِنْسِ المَرْأَةِ وَطَبِيعَتِهَا بِقَطْعِ النَّظَرِ عَنِ الأَفْرَادِ فِيهِمَا ، وَإِلَّا فَقَدْ يَتَّفِقُ أَنَّ بَعْضَ أَفْرَادِ المَرْأَةِ خَيْرٌ مِنْ كَثِيرٍ مِنْ أَفْرَادِ الرَّجُلِ. وَلَا يَصِحُ أَنْ تَكُونَ جُمْلَةُ البَسْمَلَةِ مِنْهَا ؛ لَا بِاعْتِبَارِ المُتَعَلَّقِ، وَلَا بِاعْتِبَارِ إِضَافَةِ الاِسْمِ إِلَى لَفْظِ الجَلَالَةِ؛ إِذْ لَا يَصِحُ أَنْ يُرَادَ مِنَ المُؤمِنِ مَثَلاً الجِنْسُ وَالطَّبِيعَةُ بِقَطْعِ النَّظَرِ عَنِ الأَفْرَادِ؛ لأَنَّهُ لَا يَقَعَ مِنْهُ ابْتِدَاءٌ، وَلَا يَصِحُ أَنْ يُرَادَ مِنَ الاِسْمِ الجِنْسُ وَالطَّبِيعَةُ كَذَلِكَ؛ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَقَعُ بِهِ ابْتِدَاءً. قال الأنبابي: قوله: (كَأَنْ تَقُولَ: «الرَّجُلُ خَيْرٌ مِنَ المَرْأَةِ») قال شيخنا المؤلّف: إنَّما مثلتُ بهذا المثال موافقةً لِمَا اشتهر، وإلا فالخيريَّةُ لا تُعقَلُ إلَّا باعتبار الأفراد، فالأولى التَّمثيل بـ: «الإِنْسَانُ : حَيَوَانٌ نَاطِقٌ أَوِ : الإِنْسَانُ نَوْعٌ، وَالحَيَوَانُ جِنْسُ». اهـ .
There remains from the divisions of propositions: the natural proposition (al-qadiyya al-tabi'iyya), and it is that in which judgment is made upon the genus and nature, disregarding individuals; as if you say: 'Man is better than woman.' For the intended meaning is that the genus and nature of man is better than the genus and nature of woman disregarding individuals in both. Otherwise, it may happen that some individual women are better than many individual men. And it is not valid for the sentence of the basmala to be of this type, neither with respect to the dependent (muta'allaq) nor with respect to the annexation (idafa) of the noun to the word of Majesty; because it is not valid to intend from, e.g., 'the believer' the genus and nature disregarding individuals, for he does not perform the beginning [as a nature], and it is not valid to intend from 'the name' the genus and nature similarly, because beginning does not occur by it. Al-Anbabi said: 'His statement: "as if you say: 'Man is better than woman'" - our teacher the author said: I only gave this example in agreement with what is well-known, otherwise goodness (al-khairiyya) is not understood except by consideration of individuals, so the better example would be: "Man is a rational animal" or "Man is a species, and animal is genus." '
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage defines the natural proposition, which judges the essence of a thing without reference to its individuals. The example given is 'Man is better than woman,' meaning the nature of man is better than the nature of woman. However, this example is criticized because superiority is only meaningful when comparing individuals. A better example would be 'Man is a rational animal' because that defines the nature. The author then argues that the basmala cannot be a natural proposition, because neither the believer (who begins) nor the name (which is begun with) can be taken as a nature without individuals, since beginning is an action that requires an individual agent and instrument. This lesson uses logical classification to clarify the type of proposition that the basmala represents.

Key Terms
القضية الطبيعية
الجنس والطبيعة
بقطع النظر عن الأفراد

B) 'Man is a rational animal'
C) 'The believer begins with the name of Allah'
D) 'Some men are tall'

Key Takeaway
The natural proposition makes a judgment about the essence of a thing, ignoring individuals; the basmala cannot be natural because it inherently refers to a specific agent and instrument.

Expanding the Scope of Voluntary: The Two Types of Ikhtiyari
Author addresses an objection about praising Allah's essence by expanding the meaning of voluntary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ikhtiyari haqiqatan and ikhtiyari hukman and explain how the latter allows praise of divine attributes.

Core Idea
Voluntary includes not only chosen acts but also the sources of voluntary acts, expanding praise to Allah's attributes.

In logic, the term 'ikhtiyari' is often restricted to acts of choice. However, when praising Allah, this restriction seems to exclude His essence and attributes. The commentator resolves this by expanding the definition of 'ikhtiyari' into two types: real voluntary and ruling voluntary. This lesson will show you how this logical move preserves the scope of praise.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection
The passage starts with a hypothetical objection: if 'hamd' is restricted to voluntary acts, then praising Allah's essence and attributes would be excluded, because they are not voluntary in the human sense.
This objection highlights a potential problem in the definition of hamd.
2
Extract the Two Types of Voluntary
The answer introduces two types: 'al-ikhtiyari haqiqatan' (real voluntary), which refers to actions of choice, and 'al-ikhtiyari hukman' (ruling voluntary), which includes anything that is a source of voluntary acts or concomitant to such a source.
The term 'hukman' means 'by legal ruling' or 'by extension'.
3
Understand Ruling Voluntary
Ruling voluntary is defined as 'what is a source of voluntary acts' (like Allah's essence and power) or 'what is concomitant to its source' (like Allah's hearing and sight). These are not voluntary in themselves but are treated as voluntary because they are intimately linked to voluntary acts.
This is a logical expansion based on causation and concomitance.
4
Apply the Distinction
Using this distinction, praising Allah's essence and attributes becomes valid: they fall under 'ruling voluntary'. The objection is resolved by broadening the concept of voluntary to include not only acts but also their sources and necessary concomitants.
This shows how logical tools can defend theological positions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ قِيْلَ: التَّقْيِيدُ بِـ (الِاخْتِيَارِيِّ) يُخْرِجُ : الحَمْدَ عَلَى ذَاتِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَصِفَاتِهِ. أَجِيْبَ : بِأَنَّ المُرَادَ بِـ (الِاخْتِيَارِيِّ) مَا يَشْمَلُ : - الاخْتِيَارِيَّ حَقِيقَةٌ، وَهُوَ ظَاهِرٌ. - وَالاخْتِيَارِيَّ حُكْماً ، وَهُوَ : مَا كَانَ مَنْشَأ الأَفْعَالِ الِاخْتِيَارِيَّةِ كَـ: ذَاتِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى، وَقُدْرَتِهِ، وَمَا كَانَ مُلَازِماً لِمَنْشَيْهَا كَـ: سَمْعِهِ تَعَالَى، وَبَصَرِهِ.
If it is said: The restriction with 'voluntary' excludes praise upon the essence of Allah Most High and His attributes. It is answered: That what is meant by 'voluntary' includes: the voluntary in reality, which is apparent, and the voluntary by ruling, which is what is a source of voluntary acts like the essence of Allah Most High and His power, and what is concomitant to its source like His hearing and His sight.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical exchange. An objection is raised: if hamd (praise) is restricted to voluntary acts, then praising Allah's essence and attributes (which are not voluntary in the human sense) would be excluded. The answer resolves this by distinguishing two types of 'ikhtiyari': real voluntary (which applies to acts of choice) and ruling voluntary (which applies to entities that are the source of voluntary acts or concomitant to such sources). Thus, Allah's attributes like power, hearing, sight are considered voluntary by ruling because they are sources of voluntary acts. This expands the scope of praise to include divine attributes without contradiction.

منشأ

Key Takeaway
The concept of voluntary is broadened to include not only actual choices but also the sources and concomitants of voluntary acts, allowing praise of Allah's attributes.

The Three Types of Lam in 'Lillah'
Author enumerates the nine possibilities for 'al-hamdu lillah' by combining types of 'al' and 'lam'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between lam al-istihqaq, lam al-ikhtisas, and lam al-milk, and identify which type of lam is used in a given Arabic phrase from Islamic texts.

Core Idea
Three types of lam distinguish entitlement, specification, and possession - precision in Arabic grammar.

In this passage, the author analyzes the phrase 'al-hamdu lillah' by breaking down its two particles: the definite article 'al' and the preposition 'lam'. Both have three possible meanings, leading to nine combinatorial possibilities. The focus here is on the three types of lam, each indicating a different relationship between two entities: entitlement (between meaning and essence), specification (between two essences without ownership), and possession (between two essences with ownership). Understanding these distinctions is crucial for precise interpretation of Qur'anic verses and Islamic texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two parts of the phrase
The analysis splits 'al-hamdu lillah' into the definite article 'al' on 'al-hamd' and the 'lam' on 'Allah'. Focus on the lam, which has three possible types.
The three types of 'al' are also mentioned but not the focus here.
2
Learn the definitions of the three lams
Lam al-istihqaq occurs between a meaning and an essence. Lam al-ikhtisas occurs between two essences where the object is not owned. Lam al-milk occurs between two essences where the object is owned.
Memorize the key difference: istihqaq involves meaning, ikhtisas involves no ownership, milk involves ownership.
3
Match examples to definitions
The passage gives examples: 'al-hamdu lillah' and 'waylun lil-mutaffifin' are istihqaq; 'al-jullu lil-dabbah' is ikhtisas; 'al-malu lizayd' is milk. Verify each by checking the relata and ownership condition.
Notice that in istihqaq, the first entity (e.g., hamd) is a meaning, not a physical object.
4
Apply to a new Qur'anic example
Consider 'al-arshu lillah' (Qur'an 39:75). The lam connects 'arsh (a created object) to Allah. Is it ownership? In Islamic theology, Allah owns the Throne, but it is also a sign of His majesty. However, since 'arsh is a created entity and Allah is its Creator, lam of milk is not fully fitting. Rather, it is lam of istihqaq (entitlement) because the Throne is worthy of being attributed to Allah in a unique sense.
This shows the nuance; not all phrases with 'lillah' are automatically istihqaq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَلْ فِي الْحَمْدِ إِمَّا لِلْعَهْدِ، أَوْ لِلْاسْتِغْرَاقِ، أَوْ لِلْجِنْسِ؛ وَعَلَى كُلٍّ، فَـ اللَّامُ فِي اللَّهِ إِمَّا لِلِاسْتِحْقَاقِ، أَوْ لِلِاخْتِصَاصِ، أَوْ لِلْمِلْكِ؛ فَالْاِحْتِمَالَاتُ تِسْعَةٌ قَائِمَةٌ مِنْ ضَرْبِ ثَلَاثَةٍ فِي مِثْلِهَا. الْفَرْقُ بَيْنَ هَذِهِ الثَّلَاثَةِ: أَنَّ لَامَ الِاسْتِحْقَاقِ هِيَ الْوَاقِعَةُ بَيْنَ مَعْنًى وَذَاتٍ نَحْوُ: الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ، وَوَيْلٌ لِلْمُطَفِّفِينَ. وَلَامَ الِاخْتِصَاصِ هِيَ الْوَاقِعَةُ بَيْنَ ذَاتَيْنِ وَمَدْخُولُهَا لَا يُمْلَكُ نَحْوُ: الْجُلُّ لِلدَّابَّةِ. وَلَامَ الْمِلْكِ هِيَ الْوَاقِعَةُ بَيْنَ ذَاتَيْنِ وَمَدْخُولُهَا يُمْلَكُ نَحْوُ: الْمَالُ لِزَيْدٍ.
And the 'al' in 'al-hamd' is either for covenant, or for generality, or for genus; and in any case, the lam in 'Allah' is either for entitlement, or for specification, or for possession; thus the possibilities are nine, arising from multiplying three by its like. The difference between these three: lam of entitlement is that which occurs between a meaning and an essence, e.g., 'al-hamdu lillah' and 'waylun lil-mutaffifin'; lam of specification is that which occurs between two essences and its object is not owned, e.g., 'al-jullu lil-dabbah'; lam of possession is that which occurs between two essences and its object is owned, e.g., 'al-malu lizayd'.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a grammatical-logical classification. The author first notes that the definite article 'al' in 'al-hamd' has three possible meanings: covenant (referring to a specific praise), generality (all praises), or genus (the kind of praise). Then the lam in 'lillah' also has three possibilities: entitlement (istihqaq), specification (ikhtisas), or possession (milk). The total possibilities are nine (3x3). The explanation then defines each lam: lam of entitlement occurs between a meaning and an essence (e.g., 'al-hamdu lillah' where praise belongs to Allah); lam of specification occurs between two essences where the object is not owned (e.g., 'the blanket belongs to the animal' meaning it is for its use); lam of possession occurs between two essences where the object is owned (e.g., 'the money belongs to Zayd'). This analysis shows the precision of Arabic in conveying relationships.

Key Terms
لام الاستحقاق
لام الاختصاص
لام الملك

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) الجل للدابة

Key Takeaway
The lam in 'lillah' can indicate entitlement, specification, or possession, and only careful analysis of the relationship between the two nouns determines which type is intended.

Classification of Propositions by the Quantifier 'Al'
Al-Bajuri enumerates five propositional types from the hamdalah using variations of 'al'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the five propositional types (shakhsiyya, kulliyya, juz'iyya, muhmala, tabi'iyya) that arise from different interpretations of the definite article 'al' in the hamdalah.

Core Idea
The same sentence can yield five different logical propositions based on how you read the 'al'.

In the science of mantiq, the quantifier of a proposition determines its logical type. The commentator al-Bajuri demonstrates this by analyzing the phrase 'al-hamdu lillah'. By varying the meaning of the definite article 'al', he shows how the same words can produce a particular, universal, particular, absolute, or natural proposition. This exercise reveals the precision required in logical analysis of even the most familiar phrases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five interpretations of 'al'
From the passage, list the five ways 'al' can be understood: for 'ahd (specific reference), for istighraq (universal quantification), for jins within some individuals, for jins disregarding quantifier, and for jins/nature disregarding individuals.
2
Match each interpretation to its proposition type
The passage explicitly gives the correspondence: 'ahd → shakhsiyya, istighraq → kulliyya, jins within some → juz'iyya, jins disregarding quantifier → muhmala, jins disregarding individuals → tabi'iyya.
Be careful: muhmala and tabi'iyya both use 'al' for the genus but differ in whether individuals are considered.
3
Understand the subtle differences
Muhmala disregards the quantifier but not the individuals; tabi'iyya disregards individuals entirely. This affects the logical force of the proposition.
For example, a universal proposition claims something about every individual, while an absolute proposition makes a claim without specifying quantity.
4
Apply to the hamdalah
For each interpretation, explain what the proposition would mean. For instance, if 'al' is for specific reference, it refers to a particular praise (e.g., the praise being uttered now). If universal, it means all praises are for Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(1) الحَمْدُ للهِ الَّذِي قَدْ أَخْرَجَا نَتَائِجَ الفِكْرِ لِأَرْبَابِ الحِجَا. وَعَلَى جَعْلِهَا لِلِاسْتِغْرَاقِ، أَوْ لِلجِنْسِ فِي ضِمْنِ الأَفْرَادِ؛ يَمْتَنِعُ ذَلِكَ (1) بِالنِّسْبَةِ لِلقَدِيمِ، وَلَا يَمْتَنِعُ بِالنِّسْبَةِ لِلحَادِثِ إِنْ لُوحِظَ أَنَّ الأَفْرَادَ غَيْرُ مُرَكَّبَةٍ، وَإِلَّا لَمْ يَمْتَنِعُ أَصْلاً (2)؛ لِمَا عَلِمْتَ مِنْ أَنَّ المُرَكَّبَ مِنَ القَدِيم وَالحَادِثِ حَادِفٌ. وَمِمَّا يَنْبَغِي التَّنْبَهَ لَهُ : أَنَّ الحَمْدَ القَدِيمَ هُوَ نَفْسُ الكَلَامِ القَدِيمِ بِاعْتِبَارِ دَلَالَتِهِ عَلَى الكَمَالَاتِ، فَهُوَ مِنْ أَنْوَاعِ الكَلَامِ الاعْتِبَارِيَّةِ (3) ، كَمَا هُوَ مُقَرَّرٌ فِي عِلْمِ التَّوْحِيدِ. وَقَدِ اشْتُهِرَ أَيْضاً أَنَّ جُمْلَةَ الحَمْدَلَةِ» يَصِحُ أَنْ تَكُونَ إِنْشَائِيَّةٌ ، وَعَلَيْهِ فَلَا تُسَمَّى : «قَضِيَّةٌ»؛ لِمَا مَرَّ ، وَأَنْ تَكُونَ خَبَرِيَّةٌ ، وَعَلَيْهِ فَتُسَمَّى: «قَضِيَّةٌ» ; ثُمَّ: - إِنْ جُعِلَتْ «أَلْ» فِيهَا لِلعَهْدِ، كَانَتْ «قَضِيَّةٌ شَخْصِيَّةٌ» . - وَإِنْ جُعِلَتْ لِلِاسْتِغْرَاقِ، كَانَتْ «قَضِيَّةٌ كُلِّيَّةٌ (4)) . - وَإِنْ جُعِلَتْ لِلجِنْسِ فِي ضِمْنِ البَعْضِ ، كَانَتْ «قَضِيَّةٌ جُزْئِيَّةٌ ( ه ) . وَإِنْ جُعِلَتْ لَهُ فِي ضِمْنِ الأَفْرَادِ بِقَطْعِ النَّظَرِ عَنِ الكُلِّيَّةِ وَالجُزْئِيَّةِ، كَانَتْ «قَضِيَّةٌ مُهْمَلَةٌ» (1). - وَلَا مَانِعَ هُنَا مِنْ جَعْلِهَا طَبِيعِيَّة) (2)؛ بِأَنْ تُجْعَلَ أَلْ» فِيهَا لِلجِنْسِ وَالطَّبِيعَةِ، بِقَطْعِ النَّظَرِ عَنِ الْأَفْرَادِ. وَاسْتُشْكِلَ كَوْنَهَا إِنْشَائِيَّةٌ : بِأَنَّهُ لَا يُمْكِنُ العَبْدَ أَنْ يُنْشِئَ مَضْمُونَ هَذِهِ الجُمْلَةِ وَلَا حُكْمَهَا :
(1) Praise be to Allah who brought forth the fruits of thought for people of intellect. And regarding making it for universal quantification, or for the genus within the individuals: that is impossible with respect to the Eternal, and not impossible with respect to the originated if it is considered that the individuals are not composite, otherwise it would not be impossible at all; because you know that the composite of the eternal and the originated is originated. And among what should be noted is that the eternal praise is the same as the eternal speech in consideration of its indication of perfections, so it is one of the types of consideration-based speech, as is established in the science of tawhid. And it is also well-known that the phrase 'Praise be to Allah' can be declarative, and accordingly it is not called a proposition; and it can be informative, and accordingly it is called a proposition. Then: If 'al' in it is taken for specific reference, it becomes a particular proposition. And if it is taken for universal quantification, it becomes a universal proposition. And if it is taken for the genus within some individuals, it becomes a particular proposition. And if it is taken for it within the individuals while disregarding universality and particularity, it becomes an absolute proposition. And there is no obstacle here to making it a natural proposition; by making 'al' in it for the genus and nature, disregarding individuals. And it was objected that it could be declarative: because it is not possible for the servant to originate the content of this sentence nor its judgment:
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the opening line of the matn, 'al-hamdu lillah...' The commentator, al-Bajuri, begins by discussing the implications of the definite article 'al' in 'al-hamd' when applying it to the eternal (God) and the created. He states that if 'al' is taken for universal quantification or for the genus within individuals, such attributions are impossible for the eternal because the eternal cannot be composed of parts, but for the created it is possible if the individuals are not considered composite. He then explains that 'al-hamd' as an eternal attribute is identical to the eternal speech (kalam) in terms of indicating perfections, and it is a type of consideration-based speech. Next, he notes that the phrase 'al-hamdu lillah' can be taken as a declarative sentence (insha'iyyah) or an informative sentence (khabariyyah). If declarative, it is not called a proposition (qadiyya). If informative, it is a proposition. He then classifies the proposition based on the interpretation of 'al': if for specific reference ('ahd), it is a particular proposition (shakhsiyyah); if for universal quantification (istighraq), it is a universal proposition (kulliyyah); if for the genus within some individuals (jins fi dimn al-ba'd), it is a particular proposition (juz'iyyah); if for the genus within individuals disregarding universality and particularity, it is an absolute proposition (muhmalah); and if for the genus and nature disregarding individuals, it is a natural proposition (tabi'iyyah). Finally, he raises an objection: how can a servant originate the content or judgment of this sentence, since praise belongs to God? The response implies that the proposition is about the servant's act of praising, not the eternal attribute.

شَخْصِيَّة
كُلِّيَّة
جُزْئِيَّة
مُهْمَلَة
طَبِيعِيَّة

Key Takeaway
The logical type of a proposition can change based on the interpretation of the definite article.

The Insha'iyyah vs. Khabariyyah Distinction and the Objection
Al-Bajuri discusses the insha'iyyah/khabariyyah distinction and an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between insha'iyyah (declarative) and khabariyyah (informative) uses of the phrase 'al-hamdu lillah' and understand the objection that a servant cannot originate eternal praise.

Core Idea
Not every meaningful utterance is a proposition; some are declarative acts of praise.

In the study of mantiq, only informative sentences (khabariyyah) can be true or false. Declarative sentences (insha'iyyah) are not truth-apt. The commentator al-Bajuri applies this to the hamdalah, noting that it can be taken either way. He then addresses an objection: how can a servant originate the content of eternal praise? This leads to a deeper theological point about the nature of the phrase.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
The passage states that 'al-hamdu lillah' can be insha'iyyah (declarative) or khabariyyah (informative).
2
Understand the consequence
If insha'iyyah, it is not called a proposition (qadiyya) because it is not truth-apt. If khabariyyah, it is a proposition.
3
Analyze the objection
The objection is that a servant cannot 'originate' (yunshe'u) the content or judgment of this sentence. Why? Because praise is an eternal attribute of God, and the servant's utterance cannot create that eternal praise.
4
Consider the response
The passage does not fully articulate the response, but implies that the proposition is about the servant's act of praising, not the eternal attribute. This resolves the objection.
